Common applications include molecular encapsulation, selective ion or molecule transport, gas storage (e.g., methane or hydrogen clathrates), drug delivery (by protecting and transporting active agents), and as hosts in host-guest chemistry for molecular recognition and sensing.\n\nMacrocycles, such as crown ethers, cyclodextrins, and porphyrins, are large ring-shaped molecules with an open or semi-open structure. Their applications often involve selective binding of ions or small molecules (e.g., ion transport, phase transfer catalysis), molecular recognition, catalysis (as in metalloporphyrins), and drug delivery (especially with cyclodextrins improving solubility and stability of pharmaceuticals).\n\nThere is significant overlap in their uses, particularly in host-guest chemistry, molecular recognition, and drug delivery. Both can act as hosts for smaller guest molecules or ions, and both are used in the design of sensors and separation technologies.
